* Site clearing and grading: trees, brush, and existing structures conflicting with building placement must be removed. Topsoil should be stripped and stockpiled before grading — it is valuable for finish grading later.
* Temporary construction utilities: a temporary power pole and meter may be required if permanent electric service is not yet energized. Cost: $500–$2,000 depending on utility company and distance.
* Construction access road: a temporary gravel road (crushed stone 4–6 in. on geotextile fabric) from the site entrance to the building location protects the permanent driveway and keeps mud out of the building during construction.
App fields and cascade: legal access confirmed, access road adequacy, driveway culvert permit required, clearing scope, temporary power needed. Site development items added to Build Sequence before Step 4 (site clearing) and budget added as property-level line items.
Due Diligence Cascade into Build Sequence
Build Sequence Step 1 (Site plan finalized) is blocked from Complete status until the following are confirmed:
* Boundary survey complete (property lines on site plan layer)
* Zoning confirmed (setback distances entered, permitted use verified)
* Flood zone designation recorded
* Easements recorded on site plan layer
* 811 underground utility locate completed
Build Sequence Steps 5 and 6 (underground utilities and foundation) are additionally gated by:
* Soil bearing test complete or explicitly waived with owner acknowledgment
* Wetland delineation complete if any potential wetlands exist
* Access road confirmed adequate for construction traffic


Due Diligence Module Complete When
All seven categories have a status of Complete or Not applicable. Property boundary confirmed on site plan layer. Setback zones calculated and displayed. All easements recorded on site plan layer. Flood zone designation recorded. Perc test result entered and drain field sizing updated. Soil bearing capacity result entered and foundation type updated if applicable. Wetland delineation complete or explicitly confirmed not needed. Access confirmed adequate for construction traffic. All budget line items from this module at Estimated status or higher.
5. Layout Layer Architecture
The layout plan is the master coordination document. Every decision writes a coordinate into the layout. Every trade's requirements are calculated from those coordinates. The plan is not made separately — it IS the decision record expressed spatially.


5.1 Layer Activation Rules
Layers activate automatically based on decisions already made. A simple storage barn with no utilities stays simple. Complexity appears only when decisions require it.
Layer
	Activates When
	What It Shows
	Shell
	Any project created
	Exterior walls, roof outline, doors, windows, overall dimensions
	Foundation
	Any project created
	Foundation type, perimeter, frost depth zones, anchor bolt pattern. For buildings with mixed heated and unheated zones: hybrid slab transition joint shown as a flagged line between zone boundaries — this is an engineered detail (step joint with compressible filler, differential settlement risk) that must appear on the foundation layer before the pre-pour document is generated. If a heated and unheated zone share a building and the transition joint is not placed, the tool blocks pre-pour document generation and shows a blocker: &#x201C;Hybrid slab transition joint not located — required before pour.&#x201D;
	Zones / Sections
	Any interior walls placed
	Interior walls, zone labels, thermal boundaries highlighted
	Structural
	Construction type ≠ gravel pad
	Posts, beams, load-bearing walls, headers, holdowns, LVL locations
	Electrical
	Any electrical device placed
	Panel, circuits, conduit runs, outlets, switches, sub-panels, inter-building conduit
	Plumbing
	Any fixture placed
	Supply lines, drain lines, vent stack, wet wall, sleeves, slope arrows, trap locations
	Radiant heat
	Heated floor = yes for any zone
	PEX loop layout, manifold location, zone boundaries, boiler location
	HVAC routing
	Any conditioned zone
	Mini-split locations, lineset paths, duct chases, combustion air inlet
	Gas / Propane
	Any propane appliance placed
	Line from tank, sleeves, stub-ups, shutoffs, BTU demand per run
	Solar
	Solar intent ≠ none
	Solar intent = Future or Maybe: reservation state — array zone shown as hatched outline on roof plan, no penetrations permitted inside it, no sizing calculations yet. Solar intent = Grid-Tied or Battery Hybrid: active state — full layer activates with array footprint, inverter location, battery bank, conduit to panel. Solar intent = None: layer hidden but a &#x201C;stub conduit&#x201D; reminder shown on electrical layer (costs almost nothing now, enables future solar without breaking concrete). The reservation state is the critical addition — even a Maybe solar intent locks the roof zone so no plumbing vent, lineset, flue, or exhaust fan is placed inside the future array footprint.
	Items + Appliances
	Any library item placed in a zone
	Scaled footprints, clearances, electrical/gas/water connections shown
	Pre-Pour
	Any slab zone — composite
	Everything from every trade that must be in the slab — the pour coordination document
	Septic
	Any bathroom fixture placed or septic system type selected
	Septic tank location, drain field footprint, setback boundaries (10 ft from buildings, 50 ft from well, 10 ft from property lines per Kansas standard — confirm with Miami County Health Dept), sewer line exit point from building with slope arrows, cleanout location. Drain field conflicts with underground utilities, propane tank setback, and future building envelopes shown as red flags. Perc test result drives drain field sizing. See Section 5.3 for full Septic layer spec.
	Site Drainage
	Any building placed on site plan
	Site grade arrows showing 6" drop in first 10 ft away from every building (Section 8.2 requirement). French drain locations on any uphill building face. Downspout discharge directions. Surface water flow paths. Conflict flags when drainage flows toward a foundation, toward the septic drain field, or toward the propane tank. Clay soil on this property makes this layer critical — standing water against the foundation is not a cosmetic issue, it is a slab heave risk. See Section 5.4 for full Site Drainage layer spec.
	VEHICLE PIT LAYER: activates when any zone in the building has zone type = Vehicle Service Pit. Shows: pit footprint and depth on the foundation layer, edge beam rebar detail at pit perimeter, oil/water separator location on the plumbing layer, ventilation duct sleeve on the pre-pour layer, grating/cover opening on the structural layer, GFCI outlet locations on the electrical layer. Pre-pour blockers: pit structural opening + edge beam, oil/water separator rough-in, ventilation sleeve. All three must be placed on the pre-pour drawing before pre-pour document can be generated. If pit geometry is not locked, foundation design is blocked.COLD STORAGE LAYER: activates when any zone in the building has zone type = Cold Storage / Root Cellar. Shows: cold storage room footprint and depth on the foundation layer, hatch location on the structural layer (opening in barn slab above), hatch edge beam on the foundation layer, inverted insulation notation on the ceiling surface (barn slab above cold room), no vapor barrier notation on cold storage floor surface. Pre-pour blockers: hatch structural opening + edge beam must be placed on pre-pour drawing before pre-pour document can be generated. If hatch location is not locked, foundation design is blocked.SCENARIO BUILDINGS LAYER: activates automatically when more than one Scenario exists on a Property. Shows each Scenario's building footprints on the shared site canvas in a distinct color per Scenario (Scenario A = blue, Scenario B = green, Scenario C = orange, etc.). Each Scenario's buildings are on their own toggleable sub-layer — the user can view one Scenario at a time or all simultaneously. The shared property-level elements (septic, propane tank, drainage, site utilities, Placeholder Buildings) are always visible regardless of which Scenario layer is active. Single-Scenario case: the Scenario Buildings layer does not appear in the UI at all — no new chrome, no Scenario switcher, no color coding. The first Scenario is invisible until a second is created.CROSS-SCENARIO CONFLICT FLAGS (fires when Scenario Buildings layer is active):Two Scenarios have overlapping building footprints on the same site — flag with both Scenario identities: "Scenario A Barn and Scenario B Workshop overlap. One or both must be repositioned before site work begins." Note: this is not necessarily an error — if one Scenario replaces the other at the same location it is intentional. The flag is advisory, not a blocker.A Scenario's building footprint conflicts with a shared site element — building placed inside septic drain field setback, building placed within propane tank setback, building footprint overlapping a Placeholder Building envelope. These flags use the same conflict detection logic as the single-Scenario case and are always blockers regardless of Scenario count.Layer activation is the visual result of a decision. The numeric calculations that fire from the same decision are documented in Section 9 — Decision Cascade Engine. Both sections must be read together to implement item placement correctly.


5.2 The Pre-Pour Layer — Most Critical Output
Pre-pour items by trade are detailed in this section. The document output specification is in Section 15.4. This document is generated at Build Sequence Step 7 (Section 17).
The Pre-Pour layer is generated automatically from all active layers. It is the single most consequential document the tool produces — wrong location means a jackhammer. It shows every item from every trade that must be installed before concrete is placed, on a single coordinate-accurate drawing with a checklist.


What Goes In the Slab — By Trade
Trade
	Pre-Pour Items
	Plumbing
	Drain lines with invert elevations and slope direction (1/4" per foot). Toilet flange location (12" from finished wall face, set to finished floor height). Shower drain location. Floor drain in mechanical room. Sink drain stub-ups. PEX supply sleeves through slab. Water heater cold-in sleeve. Hose bib stub-outs. Greywater separation line (if approved). SUMP PIT (if subsurface drainage ≠ None): sump pit liner set in the granular fill layer before vapor barrier and foam — 18"–24" diameter corrugated plastic or precast concrete liner, 24"–36" deep. Pit location shown on pre-pour drawing with dimension to two walls. The pit must be set before the slab is poured; cutting it in afterward requires jackhammering. INTERIOR PERIMETER DRAIN TILE (if interior system selected): 4" perforated pipe in washed gravel bed at the footing perimeter, sloped minimum 1/8" per foot toward the sump pit. Filter fabric sock required on pipe. All interior drain tile is installed before foam and vapor barrier. SUMP DISCHARGE SLEEVE: 1.5"–2" Schedule 40 PVC sleeve through the foundation wall at or above the sump pit discharge elevation, sweeping to daylight outside the building. Sleeve must be set before the footing pour on that wall. Discharge endpoint: minimum 10 ft from foundation, slope away, not toward septic drain field.
	Electrical
	Panel feed conduit (Schedule 40 PVC, sweep elbows). Sub-panel conduit. Inter-building conduit — run during site work while trench is open, always install more than you think you need. Underground service entry. In-slab conduit for any circuits crossing open slab. Floor-level junction box locations. EV charger stub conduit. Ground rod location. CONDUIT ORIENTATION RULE: all stub conduits must be oriented with sweep elbows pointing toward the panel location — not placed arbitrarily. An electrician cannot pull wire through a sweep that curves away from the panel. The pre-pour drawing shows each conduit stub with a directional arrow indicating which way the sweep faces. The tool derives this automatically from the panel location on the floor plan — if the panel location is not yet locked, conduit stub orientation is flagged as unresolved and blocks pre-pour document finalization.
	HVAC / Radiant
	PEX-A radiant loops (12" OC typical, 300 ft max per loop). Manifold location in mechanical room — position before loop layout since every loop must reach it. Zone boundaries matching thermal zone plan. Boiler supply and return locations. Condensate drain route to floor drain or drywell. Under-slab duct sleeves if forced air is used.
	Gas / Propane
	Gas line entry sleeve through foundation below frost depth (24" min Miami County). Sleeve must be sealed after line is run. Boiler/heater supply stub. Fireplace supply stub. Range stub-up location. Dryer stub-up location. Generator stub. All gas piping entering through slab requires protective sleeve.
	Structural
	Anchor bolts at sill plates (engineered pattern for Kansas wind zone). Column base plates with anchor rods. Holdowns at shear wall corners. XPS foam layout — full zone or partial depending on heated/unheated zones. Vapor barrier — 6 mil poly, seams lapped 12", taped. Perimeter insulation boards on exterior face of foundation to frost depth. Rebar schedule per engineer.
	

PRE-POUR SEQUENCE: Underground utilities → excavation + forms → foam placement → vapor barrier → under-slab rough-in from all trades → pressure test radiant PEX → inspection (required before pour) → concrete pour. Radiant PEX must remain pressurized during the pour. Assign one person to watch the gauge throughout.
Pre-Pour Sequence Enforcement:
The pre-pour document displays items grouped by installation sequence, not by trade. Items in a later sequence step that physically depend on an earlier step being complete are flagged if their predecessor is not yet checked off. Sequence dependencies the tool enforces: (1) Foam must be placed and confirmed before vapor barrier — vapor barrier cannot be installed over unplaced foam. (2) Vapor barrier must be confirmed continuous before any conduit stub, PEX loop, or gas sleeve penetrates it — every penetration through the vapor barrier requires a sealed boot, and the tool lists each penetration as a vapor barrier integrity check item. (3) PEX loops must be laid and connected to manifold before pressure test — the pressure test step is blocked until all loops are marked placed. (4) Pressure test must pass before inspection is scheduled — inspector will not sign off on an unpressurized radiant system. (5) Inspection must be signed off before pour is authorized — the pre-pour document has a final sign-off field that unlocks the &#x201C;Ready to Pour&#x201D; status. If any sequence dependency is violated, the tool shows a red blocker on the pre-pour checklist identifying which step is out of order and what must be completed first.


SIP-Specific Pre-Pour Constraints
SIP construction forces decisions earlier than standard framing. These items must be resolved before panels are manufactured:
* Window and door openings — exact rough opening dimensions locked at panel order. Cannot change after manufacture.
* Electrical chase routing decided — factory-routed channels vs. field service chase. Factory channels are precise but limit flexibility. Service chase (horizontal blocking on interior SIP face + drywall) is the standard professional solution and is fully owner-buildable.
* Outlet and switch locations on exterior walls must be finalized before panel order if using factory-routed channels.
* Penetrations for HVAC linesets, plumbing vents, and any other through-wall items must be specified at order.
* Before panels arrive on site: all window bucks must be built to exact size. Window bucks are the wooden frames inside SIP openings that provide nailing surface for windows. Cannot be added easily after panels are set.
* Bottom plate locations must be confirmed to slab layout before erection.
* Crane or wall jacks must be confirmed — large SIP panels require mechanical lifting.


5.3 Septic Layer — Full Specification
The septic layer is one of the most consequential spatial decisions on the property. The drain field location is permanent — it cannot be moved without a new perc test, new permit, and full system replacement. It must be sited before any underground utility trenching, before the propane tank is placed, and before any future building envelopes are confirmed. It is a property-level layer, not a building-level layer.
What the Septic layer shows:
Septic tank symbol with access lid location marked. Drain field footprint as a hatched rectangle — sized from perc test results and fixture count (Section 7.2 plumbing adds one fixture unit per toilet/shower/sink, rolls up to total septic load). Sewer line from building to tank with slope arrows (1/4" per foot minimum). Cleanout location accessible from grade. Distribution box location if required by system type.
Setback boundaries (shown as dashed exclusion zones):
10 ft minimum from any building foundation. 50 ft minimum from any well or water supply. 10 ft minimum from property lines. 10 ft minimum from any underground utility trench. 25 ft minimum from any stream, pond, or drainage way. These are Kansas standard minimums — Miami County Health Department must confirm local requirements before finalizing layout. The tool displays all setback zones simultaneously so conflicts are visible before any digging begins.
Conflict flags generated automatically:
Drain field inside any setback boundary. Drain field overlapping future building envelope (Placeholder Building). Underground utility trench crossing drain field. Propane tank within 10 ft of drain field. Drain field on uphill side of building (surface drainage flows toward drain field, creating saturation risk on clay soil). Sewer line slope insufficient (less than 1/4" per foot). Future house septic load not accounted for in system sizing — flag if current system is sized for barn only and future house is planned.
5.4 Site Drainage Layer — Full Specification
Site drainage is not a finish item — it is a foundation protection system. On Miami County clay soil, water that pools against a foundation wicks through the concrete and heaves the slab. The site drainage layer must be designed before grading begins and confirmed before any slab is poured. It activates as soon as any building is placed on the site plan.
What the Site Drainage layer shows:
Grade slope arrows on all four sides of every building — must show 6" drop in the first 10 ft away from the foundation on every side. French drain symbol (dashed line with chevrons) on any building face that has uphill grade running toward it. Downspout locations from the roof plan layer with discharge direction arrows — must point away from foundation and away from the septic drain field. Surface water flow path arrows showing where rainwater travels across the site. Swale locations where concentrated flow is redirected. SUBSURFACE DRAINAGE ELEMENTS (when subsurface drainage ≠ None on any building): Exterior perimeter drain tile path shown as a dashed line at footing depth around all four foundation sides, with slope direction arrows (minimum 1/8" per foot to outlet). Sump pit symbol at its placed location on the building footprint. Sump discharge pipe path from foundation wall to daylight outlet or drywell — shown as a green dashed line with outlet symbol. Discharge pipe must be shown on the site drainage layer so conflicts with other buried runs are visible. Daylight outlet location shown with a flag if within 15 ft of the septic drain field, within 10 ft of the foundation, or on a downhill slope that could reverse under saturated conditions.
Conflict flags generated automatically:
Grade slope toward foundation on any side (missing or insufficient 6"/10 ft drop). Downspout discharging toward foundation (mirrored from roof plan conflict detection). Downspout discharging toward septic drain field — saturating the drain field with roof runoff reduces absorption capacity. Surface water flow path crossing the propane tank setback zone. French drain discharging toward a neighboring building foundation. No drainage plan present when living quarters zone exists — living quarters trigger a mandatory drainage review flag before permit application. SUBSURFACE DRAINAGE CONFLICT FLAGS: Sump discharge outlet pointing toward septic drain field — concentrated discharge saturates the drain field. Sump discharge outlet within 10 ft of any foundation — water pools against the foundation it was meant to protect. Drain tile daylight outlet on the uphill side of the site — water will reverse under saturated conditions. Sump pit location not defined when subsurface drainage ≠ None — blocks pre-pour document generation. Sump discharge pipe path crossing the septic drain field footprint — drain field setback applies. No sump pit placed when site drainage condition = Low-lying and foundation = heated slab — advisory flag: "Low-lying site with heated slab — evaluate whether subsurface drainage is required before pre-pour."
5.5 Layer Interaction Model
Every layer in Section 5.1 uses the same four interaction modes. This section defines those modes once. All layer descriptions in this document refer back here rather than re-specifying interaction behavior per layer. The interaction model also defines the connection between layer geometry and materials takeoff — the layer canvas is the single source of truth for all quantity calculations. No dimension is entered twice.
5.5.1 Four Interaction Modes
Mode 1 — Draw:
Used for lines, polylines, and filled zones. Click to start, click to add vertices, double-click to close. Snap behaviors: snap-to-grid (grid size user-adjustable, default 6" for building layers, 1 ft for site layers), snap-to-existing-geometry (endpoint, midpoint, perpendicular), snap-to-setback-boundary. Draw mode is used for: wall outlines on the foundation layer, zone boundaries on the floor plan, drain field footprints on the septic layer, French drain paths on the drainage layer, solar array reservation zones on the roof plan, underground utility runs on the site utilities layer. Every drawn element immediately displays its length or area as a live label on the canvas. Undo is always available (Ctrl+Z, unlimited steps within a session).
Mode 2 — Place:
Used for dropping symbol library items onto the canvas. Single click to place at cursor position. Drag placed symbol to reposition. Symbols snap to grid and to existing geometry. Each symbol carries a default property set populated from the trade spec — a septic tank symbol defaults to the engineer-specified tank size from Section 7.2 fixture count, a panel symbol defaults to the calculated panel amperage from Section 7.1 load calc, a manifold symbol defaults to the number of zones it serves. Properties are editable after placement. Place mode is used for: septic tank, cleanout, distribution box, panel, sub-panel, manifold, PRV, propane tank, generator, downspout, French drain inlet, solar inverter, battery bank, well head. Symbol library is extensible — any item in the Section 6 item library that has a physical location on the property can be placed as a symbol.
Mode 3 — Edit Properties:
Single click on any placed symbol or drawn element opens its property panel in a sidebar. The property panel has two tabs: Spatial (dimensions, position, orientation) and Construction (type, material, spec, status, linked section). Spatial properties can be edited numerically — typing a new length updates the canvas geometry. Construction properties drive all calculations and cascade logic. Changing a construction property triggers the cascade check (Section 5.5.3) before the change is applied. Every property panel shows a &#x201C;Used in takeoff&#x201D; indicator listing which takeoff line items this element feeds — so the user always knows what will change in the materials list when they edit a property. Property panels for locked elements (Section 5.5.4) show all values read-only with a lock icon and an unlock button.
Mode 4 — Delete:
Select an element and press Delete or use the trash icon in the property panel. Simple elements (a single conduit run, a downspout symbol) delete immediately with undo available. Cascade deletions — deleting an element that other elements depend on — trigger a confirmation dialog that lists every dependent element and calculation that will be affected before the deletion is confirmed. Examples of cascade deletions: deleting a building record removes all its layer elements, all its surface records, and all its takeoff line items. Deleting a zone boundary that defines a radiant heating zone removes the manifold loop calculations for that zone. Deleting a roof surface that has a solar reservation removes the solar production estimate. The confirmation dialog for cascade deletions is not dismissable with a keyboard shortcut — it requires an explicit click on &#x201C;Delete and remove N dependent items&#x201D; to prevent accidental data loss.
5.5.2 Geometry Drives Takeoff — No Double Entry
The materials takeoff in Section 6.1 is not a form the user fills out. It is a live calculation derived entirely from layer geometry and element properties. Every dimension the user draws or places on a layer is available to the takeoff engine. No measurement is entered twice — if a wall is 24 ft long on the foundation layer, that 24 ft drives stud count, SIP panel count, ICF form count, vapor barrier linear footage, and baseboard heater length simultaneously. Changing the wall length on the canvas updates all of those quantities in real time.
Geometry-to-takeoff mapping by element type:
Wall segment (length × height, minus openings) → stud count or SIP panel count or ICF form count, insulation area, drywall area, exterior cladding area, paint area. Roof surface (area, pitch, azimuth) → roofing material square footage, underlayment area, rigid foam board quantity, rafter or purlin count, solar array capacity, overhang linear footage. Slab zone (area, heating intent) → concrete yardage, vapor barrier area, XPS foam board quantity, PEX loop footage (derived from manifold position and zone shape), wire mesh area. Window or door opening (width × height, placed on wall segment) → subtracted from wall takeoff quantities, added to window and door schedule, drives overhang projection calculation. Underground run (polyline length, depth, material) → pipe or conduit footage, trench linear footage, bedding material quantity, backfill quantity. Zone boundary (enclosed area) → flooring area, ceiling area, paint area, HVAC load calculation input, radiant loop count. Drain field footprint (rectangle area) → excavation cubic yards, gravel quantity, perforated pipe footage. The takeoff panel is always visible as a live sidebar when any layer is active — it updates in real time as elements are drawn, placed, or modified. Clicking a takeoff line item highlights the canvas element that generated it. Clicking a canvas element highlights its takeoff line items.
Waste factors applied automatically by material type: lumber +15%, concrete +10%, drywall +10%, roofing +12%, PEX tubing +10%, conduit +5%, insulation board +8%. All waste factors are editable per project in Settings. Takeoff output for a surface is suppressed until construction type is locked (Section 6.1 generation gate) — before that point the takeoff panel shows: &#x201C;Lock construction type to calculate quantities.&#x201D; This prevents mixing confirmed quantities with planning-grade placeholders in a supplier list.
5.5.3 Cascade-Aware Editing
Some property edits trigger downstream changes across multiple sections. The tool shows the user what will change before confirming the edit — not after. This applies to any edit that touches a decision field identified in Section 9 as a cascade trigger.
When a cascade-triggering property is changed, the tool pauses and shows a cascade preview panel listing: every section affected, every calculation that will re-run, every budget line item that will update, and every layer element that will be added, removed, or flagged. The user can expand each affected item to see before and after values. Two buttons only: Apply Changes (all downstream updates simultaneously) or Cancel (reverts with no changes). There is no partial apply — cascade changes are atomic. Examples: changing solar intent from None to Grid-Tied activates the solar layer, adds inverter and battery to the place library, adds conduit run to site utilities layer, updates electrical load calc, adds budget line items. Changing construction type from stud framing to SIP changes takeoff quantities, changes the knowledge package, triggers the SIP Layer 3 pre-Layer 1 gate check, and flags the pre-pour document if wall electrical rough-in was already placed assuming stud framing. Changing a zone from heated to unheated removes radiant loop calculations, removes the zone from HVAC load calc, and flags the hybrid slab transition joint requirement if an adjacent zone remains heated.
5.5.4 Layer Lock
Once a layer reaches a milestone status, its elements lock against accidental edit. Locking is per-element, not per-layer — a single element can be locked while adjacent elements remain editable. This allows late additions (adding a conduit run after the pre-pour document is generated) while protecting elements already physically in the ground or under inspection.
Lock triggers by milestone:
Pre-pour document generated — all elements on the Pre-Pour layer lock. Permits submitted — all elements on Foundation and Site Utilities layers that appear in permit drawings lock. Inspection signed off — all elements on the inspected layer lock. Pour complete (marked by user) — all slab and radiant elements lock. Construction type confirmed — the surface record construction type field locks and can only be changed via explicit override with a reason note. Layer lock status shown as a padlock icon on the layer tab. Partially locked layer shows a half-padlock icon.
Unlocking a locked element requires clicking the lock icon, entering a reason note (minimum 10 characters), and confirming through a dialog that lists what milestone locked it and what downstream items depend on it. After unlock the element displays a permanent yellow &#x201C;Modified after lock&#x201D; indicator. The reason note and timestamp are saved to the element&#x2019;s change log and appear in any regenerated pre-pour document or permit package — creating a lightweight audit trail for field changes.
5.5.5 Takeoff Export and Supplier Format
The takeoff export system produces four output formats, each serving a distinct downstream use. All exports share the same source data — the live takeoff engine — and all respect the same scope selector: single surface, single zone, single building, single trade across a building, or full property. Partial export (only elements with locked construction types) is always available and is the recommended default for supplier calls — it prevents confirmed quantities from being mixed with planning-grade placeholders in the same document.EXPORT FORMAT 1 — SUPPLIER LIST (PDF): a printable single-page document grouped by trade. Each line shows: description, specification (size, grade, material), quantity, unit (LF / SF / CY / EA / LB), waste-adjusted total, and source element ID so a supplier can ask a specific clarifying question. Waste factors shown separately from net quantities. Header includes project name, building name, export date, scope description, and planning status of the export (Confirmed quantities only / includes Roughed-in / includes Concept). Footer notes: “Quantities derived from design drawings dated [date]. Verify dimensions on site before ordering.”EXPORT FORMAT 2 — TAKEOFF CSV: a flat table with one row per line item. Columns are split into identity, structured specification, quantity, and source groups. Structured specification uses separate fields rather than a combined string — this is what makes the CSV importable into structured estimating software without manual parsing. Identity columns: itemId, revisionNumber, trade, category, description (human-readable combined string for display). Structured specification columns: spec_material (e.g. ABS, PVC, SPF, EMT, NM-B, THWN-2, UF-B), spec_size (e.g. 3”, 2x6, 1/2”, 12 AWG), spec_grade (e.g. #2, Schedule 40, 10 AWG, SEER-20), spec_finish (galvanized / bare / painted / white / stainless — null if not applicable), spec_wire_type (NM-B / THWN-2 / XHHW-2 / UF-B / USE-2 / low-voltage — populated for all electrical wire line items, null for non-electrical), spec_conduit_type (EMT / IMC / RMC / Sch40-PVC / Sch80-PVC / FMC / LFMC / ENT / None-DirectBurial / None-FreeAir — populated for electrical conduit line items and wire items to indicate installation method, null for other trades), spec_conduit_fill_pct (numeric — populated for conduit line items showing fill percentage at time of export, null for non-conduit items), product_tier (1 / 2 / 3 — specification tier per Section 6.3; 1 = generic placeholder, 2 = category spec, 3 = specific product with model number), product_manufacturer (null at Tier 1 and 2, manufacturer name at Tier 3), product_model (null at Tier 1 and 2, model number at Tier 3), spec_notes (any additional detail not captured above). Quantity columns: unit (LF / SF / CY / EA / LB / GAL), netQuantity, wasteFactor_pct, adjustedQuantity, orderQuantity (from the pack quantity engine, Section 5.5.8), orderUnit (the unit in which material is actually purchased: sticks / sheets / coils / boxes / etc.), partialPackFlag (boolean — true when orderQuantity includes a partial pack), quantityConfidence (GeometryDerived / Estimated), planningStatus, lastModified. Source columns: sourceElementId, sourceElementType, buildingId, zoneId, surfaceId, lockedAfterMilestone. Column headers are stable across schema versions — any addition, rename, or removal increments the schema version noted in the export metadata row. First metadata row (prefixed #): schema_version, export_date, project_id, building_id, scope, planning_status_filter, trade_filter. Importable directly into Excel, Google Sheets, ProEst, Buildertrend, CoConstruct, or any platform accepting tabular quantity input.EXPORT FORMAT 3 — TAKEOFF JSON: a structured export with full fidelity to the data model. Schema documented in Section 5.5.5a. Importable into the budget module to pre-populate budget line items at Concept-status unit costs. Importable into the Flask dashboard at E:\\anthony_dashboard. Contains source element IDs for every line item. Includes schemaVersion field — import checks version before processing, warns on mismatch.EXPORT FORMAT 4 — AS-BUILT SNAPSHOT: a read-only export generated after construction is complete for a phase. Quantities locked to actual installed values, not live design quantities. Created by the owner marking a takeoff export as “As-Built” and optionally editing quantities to reflect field variations. As-built snapshots carry a permanent timestamp and cannot be regenerated from the model — they are a record of what was built. Variance between design takeoff and as-built snapshot is calculated automatically as a quantity variance report, useful for calibrating future estimates.EXPORT SCOPE SELECTOR: runs before any export. Options: (1) single surface; (2) single zone; (3) single trade across a building; (4) single building; (5) full property. Trade filter is independent of scope. Planning status filter is independent of both. The combination of scope + trade filter + planning status filter is shown in the export header of every format so the recipient knows exactly what is and is not included.
5.5.5a Takeoff JSON Schema
The takeoff JSON export uses this schema. schemaVersion is incremented any time a field is added, renamed, or removed. The import function checks schemaVersion before processing and warns on mismatch without blocking the import.
Top-level object fields: schemaVersion (string, e.g. “1.0”); exportDate (ISO 8601 datetime); projectId; buildingId (null for full-property export); scopeDescription (human-readable); planningStatusFilter (Confirmed / Confirmed+RoughedIn / All); tradeFilter (array of strings, or “All”); wasteFactorsApplied (boolean); items (array of takeoff line item objects).
* Surface Record (wall) — wall assembly takeoff derives from the combination of construction type + exterior finish + WRB type + ci thickness + drainage plane method. All layers generated automatically — the owner never enters assembly layer quantities manually. Layers and quantities by assembly type: STUD + HOUSE WRAP + SIDING: house wrap (SF = wall area); house wrap cap nails or staples (1 per 2 SF; bags of 100); house wrap tape (1 roll per 100 LF of seam); siding by type — LP/fiber cement lap (SF with 10% waste; linear exposure determines courses); board and batten (SF vertical boards + SF batten strips at 16” OC); T1-11 (SF panels, 4x8 sheets); vinyl (SF with 10% waste); siding nails or screws (by type, from SF and fastener schedule for selected siding); j-channel and trim (LF from window and door perimeters + corner count); starter strip (LF = building perimeter at base course). STUD + BUILDING PAPER + 3-COAT STUCCO: building paper / Grade D kraft paper (SF = wall area + 10% overlap; sold in 500-SF rolls); metal lath / stucco wire (SF = wall area + 5% waste; 27-in x 96-in sheets; must be fastened to studs — NOT to OSB alone — stud layout must be confirmed before lath order); galvanized roofing nails or screws for lath (1 per 6” at each stud; from lath SF and stud spacing); scratch coat — Portland cement stucco (bags of 80 lb; 1 bag per 25 SF at 3/8” thickness; sold in 80-lb bags); brown coat — same material and rate; finish coat — stucco finish (bags; 1 bag per 50 SF at 1/8” thickness; color-integral or paint-grade white); control joints (LF — required at every 144 SF of stucco field, at all openings, and at all inside corners; sold in 10-ft lengths by profile); casing bead at all window and door openings (LF = RO perimeter for each opening); corner bead at all outside corners (LF = wall height per corner); weep screed at base of stucco above grade (LF = building perimeter of stucco zones); bonding agent if stucco is applied over ICF foam (gal; 1 gal per 50 SF — replaces building paper and metal lath on ICF). STUD + CI FOAM + SIDING (rainscreen): ci rigid foam board by thickness and R-value (SF with 5% waste; 4x8 sheets); foam board adhesive or long screws for attachment (from SF and fastener schedule); furring strips for rainscreen drainage gap (1x3 or 1x4 pressure-treated — vertical at stud spacing; LF = wall height x stud count per wall); long screws for furring through foam to studs (count from furring strip layout; must penetrate stud minimum 1.5” through foam thickness); siding over furring (same quantities as house wrap + siding assembly above). SIP + HOUSE WRAP OR TAPED JOINT + SIDING: SIP facing IS the structural sheathing — no separate OSB sheathing takeoff; SIP joint tape (LF = total panel joint length — all panel-to-panel seams must be taped with manufacturer-specified tape; this is the SIP air barrier); drainage mat (SF — REQUIRED between SIP facing and any stucco or siding that would trap moisture against the OSB face — Delta-Dry or equivalent 3/8” drainage mat; without this, moisture wicks into OSB and causes delamination); house wrap over drainage mat if siding is used (SF); siding quantities same as stud assembly. NOTE: wire lath fastened directly to SIP OSB is blocked — see Section 5.7.1. ICF + STUCCO OR SIDING: no WRB required on exterior (ICF foam face is naturally water-resistant); fiberglass mesh base coat for stucco on ICF (SF; 1 bag base coat per 25 SF; fiberglass mesh embedded — NOT wire lath, which will not adhere to foam); finish coat same as stucco assembly; or furring strips + any siding type (same as ci assembly but furring screws into ICF concrete core — minimum 2” penetration into concrete). METAL PURLIN: no WRB behind metal cladding (metal is the cladding and the rain screen simultaneously); building wrap or VaporWrap (SF) ONLY if an adjacent conditioned zone shares the wall; metal wall panels (SF with 5% waste; same material as roofing panels).
Takeoff line item object fields: itemId (UUID, stable across re-exports of the same element); revisionNumber (integer starting at 1, incremented each time quantity or specification changes — itemId + revisionNumber together form the unique key for external import merges; external tools update an existing line when itemId matches and revisionNumber is higher, add a new line when itemId is absent); changeLog (array of objects, each with: revisionNumber, previousQuantity, newQuantity, changeDate, changeReason — travels with every export so external tools can display quantity history without accessing the homestead planner); trade (Structural / Concrete / Roofing / Insulation / Electrical / Plumbing / HVAC / Gas / Septic / Drainage / Solar / Other); category (subcategory within trade, e.g. “Framing Lumber”, “Conduit”, “PEX Tubing”); description; specification (size, grade, material spec string); unit (LF / SF / CY / EA / LB / GAL); netQuantity (number); wasteFactor (number, e.g. 0.15 for 15%); adjustedQuantity (number); sourceElementId (canvas element ID); sourceElementType (WallSegment / RoofSurface / SlabZone / WindowOpening / UndergroundRun / ZoneBoundary / CircuitRecord / PipeSegmentRecord / LinesetRecord / RadiantLoopRecord / GasPipeSegment / ApplianceBTURecord / StructuralElement / Other); buildingId; zoneId (or null); surfaceId (or null); planningStatus (Concept / RoughedIn / Confirmed); lastModified (ISO 8601 datetime); lockedAfterMilestone (null / PrePour / PermitSubmitted / InspectionPassed / PourComplete); asBuiltOverride (null, or object with overriddenQuantity and overrideNote when in as-built snapshot mode).
5.5.6 Per-Trade Drawing Sequence
Each trade layer is drawn in a defined sequence. The sequence matters because earlier steps create the data records that later steps depend on. Drawing out of sequence does not cause errors — the tool accepts elements in any order — but may produce incomplete records (a pipe segment with no upstream fixture, a circuit with no panel assignment) that generate amber flags. The Next Decision Queue (Section 9.3) surfaces the sequence as guided steps when a new building is created.
Structural / Foundation Layer
* Step 1 — Draw building footprint outline in Draw mode. Perimeter and area calculate immediately; drive concrete footing takeoff.
* Step 2 — Draw zone boundary lines (heated vs unheated). Hybrid slab transition joint appears automatically; must be confirmed before proceeding.
* Step 3 — Draw rebar grid: longitudinal bars first, then transverse. Bar size and spacing set in property panel. Rebar footage and lap splice locations auto-calculated.
* Step 4 — Place anchor bolt symbols at sill plates. Engineered drawing upload required before anchor bolt layout can be marked Confirmed.
* Step 5 — Place post base plate symbols at structural post locations. Each post placement fires the footing auto-generation cascade (Section 9.1 — Structural post placed): (a) thickened slab zone auto-generated at post location as default; (b) post load calculated from ridge beam span — if load exceeds thickened slab capacity for Miami County clay, auto-upgraded to isolated column footing with engineer-required flag; (c) under-slab conflict check runs (PEX, drain, conduit) — PEX conflict = Tier 2 amber, drain conflict = Tier 1 red blocker; (d) post sleeve or anchor bolt record created as pre-pour item; (e) footing concrete volume (separate line from slab) or pile count (if screw pilings selected) added to takeoff. If construction type = metal post-frame and floor type = concrete slab, tool additionally prompts for grade beam path placement between posts (user-drawn, not auto-generated). See Section 8.1a for full footing type taxonomy and sizing rules.
* Step 6 — Draw XPS foam zones. Foam board area and layer count (R-10 vs R-15) set in property panel; board count adjusts.
* Step 7 — Draw vapor barrier zone. Penetration seal items auto-added to takeoff for each conduit, sleeve, and drain that intersects the barrier.
Takeoff lines created: concrete footing + slab (separately), rebar (by bar size), anchor bolts (count), XPS foam (board count by R-value), vapor barrier (SF), vapor barrier tape (LF of seams), penetration seal kits (count by penetration).
Framing Layer
* Step 1 — Draw exterior wall segments. Construction type and wall height set per segment. Stud / SIP panel / ICF form count calculates immediately.
* Step 2 — Place window and door openings on wall segments. Wall takeoff subtracts opening area. Header size auto-calculated from opening width and wall type. Window/door schedule auto-populates.
* Step 3 — Draw interior wall segments for zone boundaries. Thermal boundary flag set per wall.
* Step 4 — Draw roof surface planes on the roof plan layer. Pitch, azimuth, material set in property panel. Rafter count, roofing SF, ridge LF, hip/valley LF all calculate from geometry.
* Step 5 — Place ridge beam line on structural layer. Span drives auto-sized LVL (flagged for engineer confirmation). Post locations cascade to foundation.
* Step 6 — Place holdown and hurricane tie symbols. Hardware count adds to structural hardware takeoff.
Takeoff lines: lumber by size (LF), SIP panels (by R-value and dimension), ICF forms (by core thickness and wall height), roofing material (SF), underlayment (SF), ridge beam (LF + LVL size), headers (count by size), holdowns (count by model), hurricane ties (count), sheathing (SF), house wrap (SF).
Electrical Layer
* Step 1 — Place panel symbol. Amperage, slot count, brand, and model set in property panel. Panel face view populates in Diagram View.
* Step 2 — Place outlets, switches, and fixtures. Zone type rules auto-assign AFCI or GFCI. Each placed device creates or extends a Circuit Record.
* Step 3 — Draw home-run arcs to panel. Home-run length records in Circuit Record. Wire gauge auto-calculates. Volt-drop flag fires if run exceeds safe limit for gauge.
* Step 4 — Draw in-slab conduit runs on pre-pour layer. Sweep direction confirmed toward panel — flagged if oriented away.
* Step 5 — Draw inter-building conduit on site utilities layer. Trench footage adds to site work takeoff.
* Step 6 — Place generator inlet, transfer switch, inverter, battery bank as applicable. One-line diagram auto-populates with each placement.
Takeoff lines: wire by gauge and type (NM-B / THWN) in LF; conduit by type and size (LF); fittings estimated (1 per 10 LF + 2 per 90— bend); junction boxes (count); device boxes (count by type); devices (count by type); panel and breakers (count by type); ground rods (count).
Plumbing Layer
* Step 1 — Confirm wet wall location. Wall must be 2x6 minimum — flagged if not confirmed. Stack centerline locks; all drain slopes calculate from this point.
* Step 2 — Place fixture symbols. Each placement creates a Fixture Record. FU count adds to building tally. Drain pipe size auto-calculates.
* Step 3 — Draw drain pipe segments from each fixture to stack. Each drawn segment creates a Pipe Segment Record. Invert elevations set in property panel; slope auto-calculates and is flagged if below 1/4” per foot.
* Step 4 — Place cleanout symbols at stack base and each direction change greater than 45—.
* Step 5 — Draw vent runs from fixture trap arms to stack or AAV. Each creates a Vent Path Record. Roof penetration coordinates written to roof plan conflict detection.
* Step 6 — Place water supply symbols: PRV at service entry, shutoff valves, hose bibs. Supply runs drawn from PRV to each fixture.
* Step 7 — If sump required: place sump pit symbol on pre-pour layer. Discharge sleeve set on foundation wall. Discharge route drawn on site drainage layer.
Takeoff lines: ABS/PVC drain pipe by diameter (LF); PVC vent pipe by diameter (LF); fittings estimated (2 per segment + 1 per direction change); cleanouts (count); trap assemblies (count); AAVs (count); PEX supply by diameter (LF); shutoff valves (count); PRV assembly (1 per building); sump pit liner (count with diameter); sump pump primary + battery backup (count); discharge pipe and check valve (1 per pit).
HVAC Layer
* Step 1 — If radiant: place manifold symbol in mechanical room first. Manifold is the geometric anchor for all loop lengths.
* Step 2 — If radiant: draw PEX loop paths in serpentine pattern. Each closed loop creates a Radiant Loop Record. Manifold port assignment set immediately — this is a pre-pour blocker.
* Step 3 — Place mini-split indoor head symbols. Equipment Record created. Outdoor unit placed; lineset routing drawn, creating Lineset Record. Sleeve location coordinates written to wall penetration layer.
* Step 4 — Place boiler or unit heater if applicable. Equipment Record created. Flue/exhaust routing drawn. Combustion air duct drawn if required.
* Step 5 — Place ERV or HRV symbol. ERV/HRV Duct Records created for supply and exhaust runs. Short-circuit conflict check fires against HVAC return air grille location.
* Step 6 — Draw condensate drain routes. Condensate Drain Record created per unit.
Takeoff lines: PEX-A radiant tubing by diameter (LF); staples/clips (per LF); manifold (1, with port count); boiler/combi boiler (count); mini-split equipment (count by BTU size); lineset by diameter (LF); lineset wall sleeve (count); ERV or HRV unit (count); ERV/HRV duct by diameter (LF); condensate drain tubing (LF).
Gas / Propane Layer
* Step 1 — Place second-stage regulator symbol at building entry. Size is a placeholder until all appliances are placed.
* Step 2 — Place appliance symbols (range, dryer, boiler, heater, fireplace, generator stub). Each creates an Appliance BTU Record. BTU rating set in property panel; pipe size to stub auto-calculates.
* Step 3 — Draw pipe segments from regulator to each appliance stub. Each creates a Pipe Segment Record (Gas). Material (black iron / CSST) set per segment. CSST flag activates CSST Bonding Coordination Record.
* Step 4 — Place shutoff valve symbols at each appliance stub. Required before any appliance reaches Confirmed status.
* Step 5 — Draw underground supply line from tank to building on site utilities layer. Depth set in property panel; frost depth check fires (24” minimum Miami County). Propane tank placed on site plan with NFPA 58 setback ring.
Takeoff lines: black iron pipe by diameter (LF); CSST by diameter (LF); fittings estimated (3 per segment + 2 per tee); shutoff valves (count by size); second-stage regulator (count); gas sleeves through foundation (count); first-stage regulator at tank (1 per property); underground LP line (LF); propane tank (size in gallons); excess flow valve (1 per tank).
Pre-Pour Composite — Final Drawing Step Before Concrete
The pre-pour composite is not drawn — it is assembled automatically from all active trade layers. The user’s drawing work is done on individual trade layers. The pre-pour composite is the validation and coordination view. The only user actions here are confirming checklist items and resolving conflicts. Conflicts must be resolved on the originating trade layer, then verified cleared in the composite view. The pre-pour composite cannot be generated until all Tier 1 pre-pour blockers are resolved — this is a hard gate.
5.5.7 Takeoff Engine: Complete Field Mapping and Change Protocol
Complete Geometry-to-Takeoff Mapping by Record Type
The following mapping extends Section 5.5.2 to cover all record types defined in Sections 7.1 through 7.4a. Each record generates multiple takeoff lines. The takeoff engine re-runs the full mapping for a record whenever any field in that record changes.
* Circuit Record — wire footage reported per wire type (LF by NM-B gauge / THWN-2 gauge / XHHW-2 gauge / UF-B gauge / USE-2 gauge / low-voltage type). Conductors in conduit reported separately from free-air and direct-burial runs — these are different line items because they are purchased differently (spool pulls vs rolls). Conduit footage reported per conduit type and trade size (LF by EMT-1/2” / EMT-3/4” / EMT-1” / Sch40-PVC-3/4” / Sch40-PVC-1” / etc.); FMC and LFMC by diameter in LF. Conduit fittings per conduit type: compression fittings (EMT/IMC), threaded fittings (RMC), glued fittings (PVC) — counted separately because they are different products purchased from different suppliers. Conduit fill percentage shown per conduit segment — over-fill is a Tier 1 red flag per Section 7.1a. Device boxes (count by type); devices (count by type and tier — Tier 1 generic, Tier 2 spec, Tier 3 model); breakers (count by type). Low-voltage wire (thermostat, data, audio) reported as separate line items by wire type.
* Fixture Record — fixture rough-in kit (1 EA by fixture type); supply shutoff valves (2 EA — hot and cold); trap assembly (1 EA by type). No pipe quantities — pipe comes from Pipe Segment Records.
* Pipe Segment Record (Plumbing) — pipe by diameter and material (LF with waste factor); fittings estimated at 2 EA baseline + 1 EA per 45— direction change + 2 EA per 90— direction change + 1 EA tee per branch.
* Vent Path Record — vent pipe by diameter (LF); AAV (1 EA if vent type = AAV); roof flashing boot (1 EA if exits through roof); vent cap (1 EA).
* Equipment Record (HVAC) — HVAC equipment (1 EA by type and BTU size); mounting hardware (1 EA by equipment type); condensate trap kit (1 EA per indoor head). Electrical circuit cross-referenced — no duplicate line.
* Lineset Record — lineset by diameter (LF with 5% waste); insulation wrap (LF same as lineset); wall sleeve kit (1 EA); line set cover (LF, exterior portion only); flare fittings (2 EA per lineset).
* Radiant Loop Record — PEX-A tubing by diameter (LF with 10% waste); staples/clips (1 EA per 12” of loop length); manifold port connection fittings (2 EA per loop). Manifold generated once from zone count, not per loop.
* ERV/HRV Duct Record — duct by diameter (LF with 5% waste); duct insulation wrap if exterior (LF); duct elbows (1 EA per direction change); wall penetration sleeve kit (1 EA per exterior penetration); wall cap/grille (1 EA per exterior penetration).
* Appliance BTU Record (Gas) — shutoff valve (1 EA by pipe size); gas connector flexible section (1 EA by BTU rating); stub-up fitting (1 EA). Appliance itself cross-referenced to item library — no duplicate line.
* Pipe Segment Record (Gas) — pipe by size and material (LF with 5% waste for black iron, 3% for CSST); fittings estimated at 2 EA per segment + 1 EA per tee + 1 EA union at regulator and appliance connections; CSST bonding clamp (1 EA per segment where CSST flag = Yes).
* Structural Element Record — engineered lumber by size (LF for beams, EA for posts); structural hardware by model (count); anchor bolts by size (count, from engineered drawing when uploaded); post base plates (count).
Takeoff Change Protocol — What Happens When Plans Change
A plan change is any edit to a canvas element, record field, or property that affects one or more takeoff line items. The protocol has five stages determined by the highest milestone status of any derived line item.
* STAGE 1 — Change before any export (all derived items at Concept or Estimated status): takeoff re-calculates immediately and silently. Budget items update automatically. No user action needed.
* STAGE 2 — Change after takeoff exported but no quote yet (Estimated status, export history exists): takeoff re-calculates. Amber “Takeoff Changed Since Export” badge appears on the affected trade showing: changed element, old quantity, new quantity, export date, and a Re-export button. If a supplier was called using the stale export, a flag in the call log reads: “Takeoff quantities changed after this call — verify before ordering.” Stage 2 does not block any action.
* STAGE 3 — Change after quote is received (Quoted status): takeoff re-calculates. Tier 2 amber flag fires: “Quoted quantity no longer matches current takeoff — [item], quoted [X], current takeoff [Y]. Requote required before committing.” Budget line item steps back from Quoted to Estimated automatically. Quote amount retained in history but marked stale. Claude Prompt 2 for this item is marked stale and must be re-run with new quantities before a fresh call is made.
* STAGE 4 — Change after PO placed (Committed status): Tier 1 red flag fires before the change is applied: “This element has a Committed budget line item. Changing it may require a change order. Current committed: $[X] for [quantity]. New quantity after this change: [Y]. Proceed?” Two buttons: Proceed with Change Order (records change order note, marks line item “Change Order Pending”, stores old and new quantities and date) or Cancel. A Committed item marked Change Order Pending appears red in budget summary until a new PO amount is entered and the item is manually re-Committed. Takeoff re-calculates to new quantity; budget retains old Committed amount until resolved.
* STAGE 5 — Change to a locked element (locked after a milestone per Section 5.5.4): unlock flow fires first (reason note required, confirmation dialog). After unlock, the change follows Stage 3 or Stage 4 depending on budget status. Element shows permanent “Modified after lock” indicator. If locked after pre-pour document was generated, pre-pour document is marked stale and must be regenerated. If locked after permit submission, permit drawings are flagged as potentially inconsistent — owner must confirm with building department whether a revised drawing submission is required.
Call Log — Data Structure
The call log is a lightweight record created automatically when the owner clicks “Generate Call Script” for a supplier (Section 13.5). It anchors the Stage 2 stale takeoff warning to a specific supplier conversation. The takeoff export version active when the call script was generated is captured as a snapshot reference — any subsequent change to that takeoff can be compared against it.
Call Log Record fields: callId (UUID); supplierId; supplierName; tradeCategory; takeoffExportId (the specific export version active at call script generation — the stale detection snapshot); callDate (defaults to today, editable); callStatus (Pending / Completed / No Answer / Callback Needed); outcome (free text — what was discussed, pricing heard, lead time); quoteReceived (boolean — when true, prompts owner to enter formal quote into budget module per Section 13.6); quantitiesDiscussed (array of line item references from the takeoff export snapshot, auto-populated from the call script, editable); takeoffStaleAtCallTime (boolean — set automatically if the takeoff had already changed before the call was made); staleSinceCall (boolean — set automatically if the takeoff changes after the call record is created while callStatus is Pending or Completed without a formal quote entered).
Stale detection: when any takeoff line item changes, all call log records referencing an export containing that line item are checked. If the call is Pending or Completed without a formal quote, staleSinceCall is set true and an amber badge fires: “Takeoff changed since this call — [item], was [old qty], now [new qty]. Verify before ordering or requoting.” Once a formal quote is entered (budget line moves to Quoted status), staleSinceCall clears — Stage 3 protocol takes over.
Call log UI: accessible from (1) the regional sourcing panel, which shows a call log tab per supplier, and (2) the takeoff panel, which shows a “Call History” indicator on any line item discussed in a call. Call records are never deleted.
Downstream Ripple Matrix — What a Change Touches
When any canvas element changes, these downstream items are evaluated in order. Affected items are flagged; unaffected items are skipped silently. The cascade preview (Section 5.5.3) shows this evaluation before the change is confirmed.
* Takeoff quantities — always re-calculated first for all line items derived from the changed element.
* Budget line item status — per item: Concept/Estimated update silently; Quoted steps back to Estimated with requote flag; Committed flags change order.
* Claude Prompt 2 (regional sourcing) — marked stale if any quantity or specification in that prompt changes. Stale badge: “Quantities changed — re-run sourcing prompt before calling suppliers.”
* Claude Prompt 3 (quote comparison) — marked stale if any quoted quantity changes. Stale badge: “Quote comparison based on quantities that have since changed. Re-run after obtaining new quotes.”
* Pre-pour document — if changed element has a pre-pour flag, document marked stale. Red banner: “Pre-pour document out of date — [element] changed on [date]. Regenerate before scheduling inspection.”
* Trade packages (Section 15.5) — if changed element affects a finalized package, that package is marked stale with a badge showing what changed and by how much.
* Section view — auto-regenerates. If exported for permit, the exported PDF is flagged: “Section view exported [date]. These elements have changed since export: [list]. Verify with building department whether revised drawings are required.”
* Build sequence — if the changed element corresponds to a step already checked off, a retroactive flag fires: “Step [N] marked complete but a related element has changed. Review whether completed work still matches current design.” Advisory only, not a blocker.
* HVAC load calculation — if changed element is a wall segment, roof surface, window, or zone boundary, Manual J re-runs for affected zones. If recalculated load puts a zone more than 20% outside equipment capacity, Tier 2 amber flag fires.
* Solar production estimate — if changed element is a roof surface, production estimate re-runs. If array wattage changes, battery sizing re-runs. If change reduces available roof area below required array size, a flag fires.
* Septic fixture count — if changed element is a Fixture Record, building FU tally re-runs and septic capacity check re-evaluates.
* Gas peak BTU demand — if changed element is an Appliance BTU Record, peak BTU demand re-calculates, all affected pipe segments re-size, and tank evaporation capacity check re-runs.
Coordinate System Rule — Drawing Order Enforcement
All canvas elements on all trade layers share a single coordinate system anchored to the building footprint. The origin (0,0) is defined as the southwest interior corner of the building footprint polygon on the foundation layer, established the moment that polygon is drawn.
Enforcement rule: no trade element can be placed on any layer until the building footprint polygon exists on the foundation layer for that building. If a user navigates to a trade layer before the footprint is drawn, the Place and Draw tools are disabled with a prompt: “Draw the building footprint on the Foundation layer first.” The layer is accessible for viewing but not for drawing.
Out-of-bounds detection: once the footprint exists, any trade element placed outside the building boundary polygon generates an amber flag: “[Element] is outside the building boundary. Confirm placement is intentional (exterior hose bib, outdoor unit, propane stub) or move inside.” The owner clears the flag by setting an “Exterior” flag on the element.
Wall Cavity Conflict Detection
A wall cavity has finite physical space. Every trade element assigned to a wall occupies cavity depth. The tool tracks cavity occupancy per wall segment and fires a conflict when total assigned depth approaches or exceeds available space.
Available cavity depth by wall type: 2x4 stud — 3.5”; 2x6 stud — 5.5”; 2x8 stud — 7.25”; SIP panel — service chase depth only (1.5”—3.5” depending on chase configuration, no cavity behind foam face); ICF — surface mount only, no cavity.
Approximate outside diameter by element type: 14 AWG NM-B — 0.48”; 12 AWG NM-B — 0.55”; 10 AWG NM-B — 0.65”; 1/2” EMT conduit — 0.71”; 3/4” EMT — 0.92”; 1/2” PEX supply — 0.62”; 3/4” PEX supply — 0.875”; 1.5” ABS/PVC drain — 1.9”; 3” ABS/PVC drain — 3.5” (fills a 2x4 cavity alone — requires 2x6 minimum); 4” ABS/PVC drain — 4.5” (requires 2x6 minimum, no other elements); 3/8” lineset suction with insulation — 1.25”; 1/2” black iron gas — 0.84”; 3/4” black iron — 1.05”.
Conflict detection: when an element is assigned to a wall segment, the tool sums outside diameters of all assigned elements and compares to available cavity. At 80% full: amber warning “Wall cavity at [wall ID] is [X]% full — verify all elements can be installed without interference.” At 100%: Tier 1 red flag “Wall cavity overloaded — assigned elements exceed available depth. Reduce elements, increase wall depth, or use surface-mount.” Flag lists every element with its diameter. Resolution options shown: upgrade framing dimension, move element to adjacent wall, or use surface-mount conduit.
Wet wall exception: the wet wall enforcement (2x6 minimum for any wall carrying a 3” or larger drain, Section 7.2) fires separately and earlier — at the moment drain size is calculated from fixture units, before other elements are assigned. The cavity conflict check is in addition to, not instead of, the wet wall framing check.
5.5.8 Pack Quantity and Cut Optimization Engine
The takeoff engine reports two distinct quantities for every line item: net quantity (what the design requires) and order quantity (what you actually buy given how materials are sold). These are always different and must be shown separately. A plumber needing 23 LF of 3” ABS buys 3 sticks (30 LF), not 23 LF. Showing only 23 LF causes confusion at the supplier counter and incorrect budget pricing. The pack quantity engine performs this conversion automatically for every material using its sold-as unit.
Sold-As Units by Material Category
* Dimensional lumber (2x4, 2x6, 2x8, etc.) — sold by the stick in standard lengths: 8, 10, 12, 14, 16, 20 ft. Engine selects the most efficient standard length for each run, minimizing offcut waste. Reports total sticks needed by length, not total LF.
* ABS / PVC drain pipe and PVC/CPVC/copper supply pipe — sold in 10-ft sticks. Order quantity = ceiling(adjusted LF / 10), reported as number of sticks. Partial sticks flagged: “Last stick: [X] ft used, [10-X] ft offcut — usable on another run.”
* PEX tubing — sold in 100-ft coils (standard) or 300-ft job coils. Engine recommends job coils when total footage exceeds 200 ft. Each individual radiant loop must fit within one coil without a mid-loop splice — loops that would require a splice are flagged.
* Electrical wire — pack quantities vary by wire type and installation method. NM-B (Romex): sold in 25, 50, 100, and 250-ft rolls by gauge. Engine selects the most efficient roll size per circuit and optimizes across circuits of the same gauge to minimize total rolls ordered. THWN-2 and XHHW-2: sold by the foot off a spool at electrical supply houses, or in 500-ft and 1000-ft spools. Order quantity reported as LF per gauge per wire type. The engine groups all conductors of the same gauge and type across all conduit runs in the building and reports total LF as a single order line with a note: “Pull from [N]-ft spool — [X] ft for circuit runs plus [Y] ft waste/offcuts.” When multiple circuits share a conduit, all conductors for that conduit are listed together with the conduit segment ID so the electrician knows which wires go in which conduit. UF-B: sold in 25, 50, 100, and 250-ft rolls by gauge, same as NM-B. Reported as a separate line item from NM-B even at the same gauge because they are different products purchased separately. Each UF-B run must be a single continuous piece — the engine reports individual run lengths, not an aggregate total, so the owner knows the longest single run and can confirm the roll size covers it without a splice. USE-2: sold by the foot off a spool or in fixed-length rolls. Reported as LF per gauge. Solar array wiring USE-2 is a separate line from building wiring USE-2. Low-voltage wire: sold in 50, 100, and 250-ft spools by wire type. Reported as LF per wire type (thermostat wire / Cat6 / speaker wire separately). Engine selects the most efficient spool size per wire type.
* EMT / rigid conduit — sold in 10-ft sticks. Same calculation as drain pipe. Conduit straps sold in boxes of 25 or 50 — order quantity = ceiling(strap count / box quantity), reported as number of boxes. Default strap spacing: 1 per 6 LF (NEC minimum). Default box size: 50-count. Both editable in Settings.
* XPS foam board — sold in 4x8 sheets (32 SF). Net SF / 32 = sheet count (ceiling). Partial sheets flagged as usable offcuts.
* Rebar — sold in 20-ft lengths. Engine calculates a cut list from the rebar map: required cut lengths are sorted and optimized into the minimum number of 20-ft sticks using bin packing. Offcuts under 2 ft treated as waste. Cut list included in the foundation trade package for pre-cutting before placement.
* Black iron pipe (gas) — sold in 21-ft lengths or cut-to-length. Order quantity = ceiling(adjusted LF / 21) reported as number of lengths. CSST — sold by the foot off a roll; order quantity reported as LF.
* Drywall — sold in 4x8 (32 SF) or 4x12 (48 SF) sheets. Engine selects sheet size based on ceiling height (4x12 preferred for 9”—12” walls to minimize seams).
* Lineset — sold by the foot or in pre-charged kits at fixed lengths (15, 25, 50 ft). If kit: order quantity = 1 kit at the next standard length above the measured run. If by foot: order LF as calculated. Engine flags if run length exceeds maximum lineset length for the equipment model.
* Insulation batts — sold in bags by coverage area (SF) at a specified R-value and stud spacing. Engine matches batt product to wall type and stud spacing, calculates net SF plus waste factor, divides by bag coverage area. Partial bags flagged.
* Fittings (all trades) — sold individually. Order = derived count + 5% overage buffer, rounded up. Couplings, elbows, tees, wyes, end caps, conduit bodies, reducers — all ordered this way. No pack-size optimization; individual unit pricing.
* Wire nuts — bags of 25 or 50 by size/color. Order = ceiling(count / bag size): red (14—12 AWG), yellow (12—10 AWG), orange (10—8 AWG). Separate line per size.
* Screws and nails: nails by the pound in 1, 5, or 25-lb boxes; engine picks most economical. Screws in boxes of 50, 100, 250, or 500; engine picks most economical. Partial boxes flagged.
* PVC primer, PVC cement, ABS cement — 4-oz, 8-oz, or 16-oz cans. Order = ceiling(joint count / 40) cans each. Primer and cement are separate lines — both required for every PVC joint. Partial cans flagged.
* Curing compound, form oil, concrete sealer — 1-gal and 5-gal pails. Order = ceiling(calculated gallons / pail size); 5-gal pail when total exceeds 3 gallons.
* Sealants and tapes (LP-rated Teflon tape, house wrap tape, flashing tape, foam sealant) — sold by roll or tube. Each type a separate line. Order = ceiling(estimated LF or joint count / coverage per unit). Partial rolls and tubes flagged.
Offcut Tracking and Cross-Run Optimization
When a material generates a partial pack, stick, or coil, the offcut is tracked as a reserved remnant and applied against the next run of the same material and diameter before a new unit is ordered. Remnants shorter than the minimum useful length for that material (2 ft for pipe and lumber, 6” for foam board, 10 ft for wire) are dropped and counted as waste.
The order quantity panel shows, for each material: net quantity, waste-adjusted quantity, remnants applied (subtracted from order), final order quantity, order unit, and a plain-language summary line. Example: “3” ABS drain pipe: 23.4 LF needed + 10% waste = 25.7 LF. Remnant from bathroom run: 4.3 LF applied. Order: 22 LF — 3 sticks of 10 ft (30 LF purchased, 8 LF offcut remaining).”
5.5.9 Takeoff Delta Export
A delta export shows only what changed between two points in time: items added, items removed, and items whose quantity or specification changed. This is the document handed to a subcontractor when scope changes after their initial quote: “here is what changed since your quote, please requote these items.”
Delta export is triggered from the takeoff export panel by selecting “Export Delta” and choosing a baseline and current state. The delta engine compares takeoffs using itemId as the stable key. Items with matching itemId but higher revisionNumber are shown as MODIFIED. Items in current state with no baseline match are ADDED. Items in baseline with no current match are REMOVED.
Output (PDF, CSV, and JSON all support delta mode): each line tagged ADDED / REMOVED / MODIFIED. Modified items show old quantity, new quantity, quantity delta (signed), old and new specification, and date changed. The PDF delta report includes a trade summary line: “Plumbing: 3 items added, 1 removed, 4 modified. Net cost impact: Estimated +$[X] at current unit prices.” Cost impact uses the most recent Claude Prompt 2 unit price, flagged as an estimate if no actual quote exists for delta items.
Baseline reference options: (1) a specific prior export by date — all exports stored in export history; (2) the state at a build sequence milestone (e.g. “as of permit submission”); (3) the state at a budget status transition. Most common use case — “what changed since the builder got our last brief” — is satisfied by selecting the most recent Builder Introduction Brief export date as the baseline.
5.7 Exterior Wall Assembly Library
The wall assembly library defines every valid combination of construction type, WRB, drainage plane, and exterior finish for this project. When construction type and exterior finish are selected on a Surface Record, the assembly library auto-populates all intermediate layers, assigns the correct vapor retarder class, and generates the complete takeoff for that wall face. No assembly layer is entered manually — the selection of two fields drives everything else. The library is the single source of truth for wall assembly decisions; the incompatibility matrix (Section 5.7.1), the assembly wizard (Section 5.7.2), and the video library (Section 5.7.3) all reference it.
Vapor Retarder Class Assignment — IECC Zone 4A
Kansas is IECC Zone 4A (mixed-humid). Vapor drive is inward in summer (hot humid exterior pushing vapor into the cooled interior) and outward in winter (warm interior pushing vapor toward cold exterior). A Class I vapor retarder (poly sheeting, foil-faced foam) on the interior of a Zone 4A wall creates a double-trap: winter condensation can’t escape outward through the retarder, and summer vapor can’t escape inward through it either. The correct Zone 4A interior retarder is Class II (kraft-faced batts, 0.1—1.0 perm) or Class III (latex paint, 1—10 perm). Class I on the interior is flagged as a Tier 1 red conflict for any stud-framed wall in Zone 4A.
* Stud framing, any siding — Class II vapor retarder (kraft-faced batts) on interior face of exterior walls. Class III (latex paint) acceptable when exterior sheathing has perm rating above 10 (e.g. fiberboard or Zip System with taped joints). Class I poly sheeting on interior: BLOCKED in Zone 4A per Section 5.7.1.
* SIP panels — no interior vapor retarder needed. The SIP panel itself is a Class II assembly — the OSB facings are semi-permeable. Do not add a poly vapor barrier to the interior of SIP walls.
* ICF walls — mass wall exemption under IECC 2018 Section R702.7.1. No vapor retarder required on ICF walls. The foam core itself provides moisture management. Flagging a vapor retarder on an ICF wall generates an advisory: “ICF walls are exempt from vapor retarder requirements under IECC 2018 R702.7.1. Adding an interior vapor retarder to an ICF wall may trap moisture in the assembly.”
* Metal purlin — vapor retarder placed on the warm side of any insulation, between insulation and interior finish. Class I poly is acceptable here because metal buildings are not airtight and the assembly can breathe at the metal panel joints.
WRB and Drainage Plane Rules by Assembly
* Stud framing + any siding: house wrap (WRB) required as a minimum. Grade D building paper (2-layer) is an acceptable alternative for stucco assemblies only. Taped OSB sheathing (Zip System) can serve as both WRB and air barrier when all seams and penetrations are taped — no separate house wrap needed. When ci foam is present outside the sheathing: the ci foam IS the drainage plane if it is a closed-cell product; open-cell foam requires a separate drainage mat or house wrap outboard of the foam.
* SIP panels: SIP joint tape is the WRB and air barrier — no separate house wrap needed. Drainage mat (Delta-Dry or equivalent) REQUIRED between SIP OSB face and any stucco or siding applied directly against the face. Without it, moisture wicks into the OSB and causes delamination within 3—7 years.
* ICF exterior: no WRB needed on the exterior foam face — ICF foam is naturally water-resistant. Drainage mat or furring strip gap recommended before any siding to allow drainage behind cladding.
* Metal purlin: no WRB needed behind metal cladding. If a conditioned zone is immediately adjacent (shared wall between workshop and equipment bay), add a VaporWrap or equivalent on the warm side of any insulation in the dividing wall.
5.7.1 Incompatibility Matrix
The following combinations are blocked before the selection is confirmed. When a blocked combination is attempted, the tool displays a plain-language explanation of why it will fail, the failure mode (structural, moisture, code), and a corrected alternative. The owner cannot proceed past a blocked combination without selecting the alternative or entering a manual override with an engineer’s note. All blocks are Tier 1 red.
* Wire lath / metal lath fastened directly to SIP OSB facing — BLOCKED. Why: SIP panels have no studs. Wire lath fasteners driven into OSB alone will pull through under the weight of three coats of stucco within 1—3 years, causing the stucco to crack and delaminate. Failure mode: structural. Corrected alternative: add continuous nailer blocking between panels at stud spacing before applying lath, OR use a fiberglass mesh base coat system (no wire lath) with a drainage mat, which is the standard SIP stucco detail.
* Stucco (3-coat with wire lath) directly on SIP OSB without drainage mat — BLOCKED. Why: the building paper or house wrap layer that normally drains moisture behind stucco cannot be reliably lapped and sealed against SIP OSB facing. Moisture from the scratch coat wicks into the OSB face and causes panel delamination and mold. Failure mode: moisture. Corrected alternative: install Delta-Dry drainage mat over the SIP joint tape before building paper and lath.
* Non-fire-rated door between garage zone and living quarters — BLOCKED. (IRC R302.5.1)
* No fire-rated drywall (5/8” Type X) on garage-side of shared wall — BLOCKED. (IRC R302.6)
* HVAC return air duct penetrating the garage-to-living separation wall — BLOCKED. (IRC M1601.6)
* Class I vapor retarder (poly sheeting, foil) on interior face of stud-framed exterior wall in IECC Zone 4A — BLOCKED. Why: double vapor trap. Summer vapor drive is inward in Kansas — hot humid exterior air pushes moisture toward the cooled interior. A Class I retarder on the interior traps this moisture in the wall cavity between the retarder and the exterior sheathing. Failure mode: moisture, mold, structural rot over time. Corrected alternative: Class II (kraft-faced batts) or Class III (latex paint on drywall). Code basis: IECC 2018 R702.7.
* Vinyl siding face-nailed flat to SIP OSB facing without furring strips — BLOCKED. Why: SIP OSB will absorb moisture behind vinyl’s lapped joints during rain. No drainage path exists.
